[26](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

Also in compositions such as a perpetuum mobile, toccata, etc.

[27](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

To consider that rhythm equals metre is nonsense; an absolutely metrical pulse would be possible only in a corpse.

[28](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

Incidentally, rubato almost always means first an acceleration; passionato (especially in recitative) very frequently requires first a ritardando, followed by an accelerando.

[29](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

Let me recall Billow’s saying which heads this chapter: “The musician’s bible begins with the words ‘In the beginning there was rhythm’. ”

[30](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

A memorable instance from my own experience. I was playing Beethoven’s Fifth Piano Concerto with a rather indifferent orchestra. In the last movement, the bassoon simply could not play the figure

![](attach/00049.png)correctly. He played not

![](attach/00081.png)but worse still![](attach/00148.png)etc. So I sang for him several

times “Klem—perer, Klein—perer” and “Ams—terdam” on these notes, with a very energetic accent on the first syllable (a well-known method used by conductors) and he got it right. Of course, I also played it on the piano.

[31](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

To make the picture complete the left hand should have been changed to: ![](attach/00120.png)

[32](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

It is obvious that the first method I indicated, namely the arithmetic method, which is suitable only for the simplest cases of polyrhythmia is a method of reasoning and analysis, while the second method is one of wisdom and synthesis.

[33](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

Remember the rendering of Rachmaninov’s “Vocalise” by Nezhdanova. (Famous operatic soprano, ed. )

[34](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

Not of the music itself, of course, which is quite different in the

extreme movements, but its performance.

[35](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

A typical example was Vladimir Pachmann who was a famous pianist in his time.

[36](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

I know them only from records.

[37](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

Title of collection of essays edited by Asafiev Calias Glebor published in 1923 and also of Yearbook published in Leningrad in 1925, 1926 and 1927, ed.

[38](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

8 1884-1950; most outstanding Russian music critic and author of books on Russian music and composers, ed.

[39](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

The same applies to dynamics: one may not confuse Mary Parsons (mp) with Mary Fields (mf), or Peter (p) with Peter Peterson (pp) or Fred (f) with Freddy Frost (ff). These childish jokes, believe it or not, are sometimes very useful even with adults.

[40](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

Famous director and co-founder of the Moscow Arts Theatre (1863-1938), ED.

[41](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

It would be more accurate to say: working at “time tone”, since rhythm and force are inseparable.

[42](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

Pre-revolution weight = 20 kg roughly.

[43](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

Richard Strauss conceived some of his operas while playing cards.

[44](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

The symbols F (force), m (mass), v (velocity), h (height) I have borrowed from physics and mechanics. They are a great help for understanding and using the physical possibilities of the piano, considered as a mechanism.

[45](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

I will not go into the purely mechanical reasons for this phenomenon. Any good piano tuner can explain this just as well, and perhaps even better.

[46](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

Russian symbolist poet 1880-1921, ed.

[47](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

Of course, everything in its proper place. The piano is also adapted for all sorts of toccata effects and even “xylophone” effects, just as much as for a moving cantilena.

[48](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

One very knowledgeable person once called my playing “stereoscopic” and this gave me very sincere satisfaction; so my efforts had, apparently, not been in vain.

[49](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

I should like to call it “inter-instrumental”; forgive the clumsy word.

[50](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

Of course, only under the baton of a great conductor. The persimfans for instance has never been a solo instrument.

persimfans (PERvyi SIMFonicheskii ANSambl First Symphonic Ensemble) functioned in Moscow from 1922 to 1932 and achieved international fame. It was an experiment in musical “collectivism” —an orchestra without conductor, ed.

[51](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

From the Ode to God by Derzhavin (1743-1816), a poem translated into most European languages, ed.

[52](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

La souplesse avant tout, as Chopin and Liszt used to say and as all knowledgeable people still say to this very day.

[53](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

3 That excellent French expression: jeu perlé.

[54](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

Russian painter 1865-1911, ed.

[55](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

As I have already said, the condition sine qua non for a good tone is complete freedom and relaxation of the arm and wrist from the shoulders to the tips of the fingers which should always be at the ready, like soldiers at the front. (After all, the decisive factor for tone quality is the contact of the fingertips on the keys; the rest—hand, wrist, arm, shoulders, back—that is “behind the lines” and must be well organized. )

[56](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

Compare the excellent indications of Hans von Bülow to the Adagio in Beethoven’s Sonata op. 106 (where the right hand has demi-semiquavers), or the second movement of op. 111 (fourth variation with demi-semiquavers).

[57](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

A typical example of this triple-level are the Choral Preludes of Bach in E flat major and C major for organ, arranged by Busoni.

[58](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

Richter plays this extremely clearly and expressively, not only because of his tremendous musical talent but also because of his tremendous, powerful hands. In such places small hands must always try to “cheat”.

[59](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

I suggest that everyone should immediately draw up a mental list of passages from piano literature (and also studies) substantiating my statement.

[60](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

A pupil of Chopin who later edited Chopin’s works, ed.

[61](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

There is a pianist who is an excellent musician and a master of his art, but I have one objection to make to his playing: h and v are exaggerated.

[62](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

Please remember once and for all that when I speak of the “knowledge” of an artist, I have always in mind an active force: understanding plus action. Or simpler still: acting correctly on the basis of correct thinking.

[63](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

If I were not afraid of making this chapter excessively long I would set down here some considerations as to why teaching of the Bach type is a thing of the past although it has lost none of its value. Let me give just two reasons: the gigantic development of music and of piano literature and its tremendous variety, similar to the variety of science. (Kant taught at the University of Königsberg all the sciences known at the time. ) In a certain sense Bach developed virgin land.

[64](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

I am almost certain that Liszt, too, was guilty of this in his young days. Remember what Glinka said of him.

[65](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

In such cases many pianists (Rachmaninov) swing their hand, arm and shoulder not only in order to feel full freedom but also in order to get the maximum swing of hand and fingers in a strict legato. Artur Schnabel in such cases even used a vibrato of the hand as if the piano were a bowing instrument. I consider this unnecessary since, as we all know, no amount of shaking the hand after a note has been played can have any effect on the sound.

[66](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

A pianist ought to be able to do the following gymnastic exercise: place his ten fingers on the floor and raise his body vertically. This is the full load which the fingers should be able to bear (these pillars, columns, arches, supporting a dome).

[67](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

Heinrich Heine: Heimkehr aus der Fremde (Yet the castrati complained / As soon as I raised my voice / They complained and they said / That I sang far too coarsely), ed.

[68](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

Muscles that turn the palm downwards, ed.

[69](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

Muscles that turn the palm upwards, ed.

[70](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

More accurately still: I taught freedom of physical movement but did not teach psychological, musical freedom. Inexperienced teacher that I was, this was a task still beyond my capabilities, and hence it was beyond the pupil’s.

[71](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

How difficult it is to describe accurately this very simple process, and how easy it is to show it on the piano with just a few words of explanation!

[72](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

The greater the volume of sound the more swing is required.

[73](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

Even this has to be said. I had a pupil once, a very practical and smart young man in everyday life, who always managed to get his way but who was rough and clumsy at the piano. I often asked him: How is it that you manage so well in your life and so badly at the piano? Then followed, of course, advice. But as far as “life” is concerned, it was he who gave me advice... which I did not follow.

[74](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

They can even be reasonably exaggerated.

[75](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

At the same time such compositions as, for instance, the Chopin concertos hold no physical difficulties for my hand.

[76](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

That same fall which, as I said earlier, produces a great volume of tone without any physical effort.

[77](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

The natural and justified desire to find a common denominator, the “original cell” of a complex phenomenon sometimes leads to amusing misunderstandings. Thus I sometimes heard teachers not unacquainted with questions of methodology say that “one should somehow be able to play a single note well, and then one can play everything well”. If this isn't black magic, may I drop dead!

This is a case where an observation which is fundamentally correct

[78](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

For instance while you are learning the E flat major scale it is a prefabricated part; when you play it, let us say, at the end of Beethoven’s Fifth Piano Concerto, it is the finished article, because it is music.

[79](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

It need not at all be the same note (key); one could for instance alternate black keys with white, change the register, use the pedal or not, but the note should, in my opinion, be isolated from any context.

[80](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

Some may object: “Yes, that may be so, but only if you have a wonderful instrument. But where will the ‘wonderful tone of the piano’ come from, when one has so frequently to play on ghastly old upright pianos? ” Those who say this don’t know the piano. However horrible the original sound may be at first—the moment when the hammer hits the string, the rasping, jangling of loosened keys and other similar delights—what follows—the vibration of the string after it is hit—is good even on the most revolting instruments. Try it and see!

[81](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

I recommend that each exercise be played every conceivable way: from pp to ff from largo to presto, from legatissimo to staccato, etc.

\* Of course in leaps and jumps the finger has quite a different task: that of grasping the right key in “mid-air” as it were.

[82](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

Incidentally this proves what actually does not require proof; that I am not a virtuoso pianist but simply a musician who knows the piano and can express himself on it.

[83](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

For more detail on this see Preface to this edition.

[84](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

I repeat my advice: dig the tunnel from both ends, never lose sight of the beginnings and the ends.

[85](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

The main thing in double notes is precision of sound, the proven simultaneous sounding of both notes. Then, as in all passages— evenness, smoothness, mastery of nuances, bringing out where necessary the upper or lower parts, etc.

[86](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

Meaning the poetic form: AB, AB, AB, CE.

[87](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

Rimsky-Korsakov said of this composition: “here the very harmony sings”.

[88](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

Forgive this metaphorical expression. In actual fact a physical collision is impossible. I merely wanted to stress the wrong relation of the fingers to the keyboard when the key is approached sideways.

[89](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

But birds, angels and other feathered creatures have wings growing from the same place as our arms, so I consider it justified to talk of flying.

[90](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

One of my teaching “peculiarities” is the advice to replace a number of Czerny and Clementi études by a selection of “motor” preludes from the Wohltemperiertes Klavier. Here is this selection: Book I, Preludes Nos. 2, 3, 5, 6, 10, 11, 14, 15, 17, 19, 20, 21; Book II, Nos. 2, 5, 6, 8, 10, 15, 18, 21, 23. Only twenty-one preludes in all! Learn them—it will enable you to “save” yourself at least fifty highly useful études. I know that this advice will arouse a certain amount of displeasure in teaching circles; nevertheless I tender it.

[91](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

Composed in 1940, ed.

[92](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

[93](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

[94](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

It would mean that I am not the only one who says so, many others say so: one head is good, two heads are better than one, but a thousand heads—that is excellent!

[98](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

This second principle is, in actual fact, merely a variant of the first, but I consider it so important that I prefer to stress it.

[99](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

For those who doubt whether this fingering is suitable for very small hands, let me say: there is no hand so small that it cannot do this. The guarantee: flexibility, suppleness, freedom and accuracy.

[100](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

That is why “repetition is the mother of learning”.

[101](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

My advice: never take on trust any editor’s fingering. And study lovingly the fingering of great composer-pianists such as Liszt, Rachmaninov, Medtner and others.

[102](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

Of course so as not to detract for an instant from the clarity of the polyphonic texture. If, in any of the parts we suddenly hear two notes, in my class this sad occurrence is termed ventriloquism.

[103](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

Not excluding his Album d’enfants.

[104](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

\* We all of us constantly use this preliminary pedal, sometimes even without realizing it.

[105](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

[106](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

[107](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

a Famous piano teacher at the Moscow Central Music School, attached to the Moscow Conservatoire, founded in 1932, ed.

[108](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

The greater, broader and more democratic the culture, the more frequent is the appearance of talent and genius. A learned man once referred to the paintings of the Italian Renaissance as an epidemic of genius.

[109](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

This is a very touching, maternal but wrong, feeling. I remember that when Glazunov was about fifty his mother used to tell the washerwoman to be “careful with the child’s linen”. The funniest thing is that when he was seventeen, Glazunov wrote a symphony which was anything but childish.

[110](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

But all this of course in a concentrated, compact, “portable” form, and ad hoc!

[111](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

The possession of a good voice is frequently mistaken for natural musicality and artistic talent. Yet we do not tend to consider a young pianist musical mainly because he happens to have a good Bechstein grand at home.

[112](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

Hence the conclusion: “compulsory piano” should be particularly compulsory for singers.

[113](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

In actual fact the reason was partly outside my control. I was, at that time, director of the conservatoire and led an extremely busy life. I had twenty-five pupils and naturally had to give more time and effort to the weaker than to the better ones (a truth of which many teachers, particularly ambitious ones, seem unaware; they work really seriously with only two or three of their most gifted pupils leaving the rest to drift in their wake).

[114](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

Here is an example from the “higher spheres”. Liszt who had recognized at once how outstandingly gifted the young Rubinstein was, refused to teach him, yet he willingly took on much less gifted pianists.

[115](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

The Circle performed all the Mahler symphonies, the Miaskow-ski symphonies, several Wagner operas, works by Richard Strauss, Debussy and several new works by Soviet composers.

[116](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

Everyone knows what this “else” is: temperament, rhythm tremendous willpower, purposeful rendering, “penetrating” and virtuoso brilliance, beautiful tone, etc.

[117](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

Incidentally, if Godowsky had four to five wrong notes in a recital, they stuck in one’s memory like so many nails hammered into the brain, whereas with Rubinstein the audience frequently failed to notice wrong notes.

[118](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

1739-1791 ED-

[119](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

This does not mean that I do not imagine with this music sometimes something entirely different: for instance, a walk along the banks of the Rhine on a spring morning... etc.

[120](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

It is markedly individual, as everything Busoni did.

[121](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

The feeling of well-being, of affinity and at the same time of an individual person (if one may so express oneself) is present here in every harmony.

[122](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

For me every good recapitulation is like a return to the homeland after a long journey.

[123](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

I stress this deliberately: there are composers who do not “fall into error” for the simple reason that they do not dare, they are retrograde. (In other words they are themselves an error. ) Whoever does not create anything new cannot create a great work of art. [This remark clearly alludes to the attacks on Shostakovich in 1936 and in 1948 and the following years, ed. ]

[124](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

Usually such pupils subsequently became very good teachers and methodologists.

[125](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

I could say a great deal about this conscience which is also good taste.

[126](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

An amusing detail. I used to weep buckets over it when I was six years old and I can still not listen to it without tears.

[127](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

The Fugue from op. 106 or the Fugue for the String Quartet op. 133, I sometimes call in petto “a banquet of the mind, an intellectual orgy” and it is precisely this that gives them their emotional and musical foundation.

[128](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

For the sake of accuracy, however, I must say that in the last few years cases of amnesia during auditions and examinations have become more frequent even among good pupils; I attribute these cases solely to the excessive work-load and fatigue during examination periods. I once had an excellent pupil who did not once play in public without forgetting and losing her place. The reason was that she was absolutely overworked and was in a constant state of fatigue.

[129](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

Here is a small example: One morning I had to adjudicate at a conservatoire competition in which nine pianists played nine sonatas by Soviet composers, after which, of course, I had to discuss their performance at length, and in the evening I played a most

[130](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

An imaginary poet, reputed for his aphorisms, invented by Count A. Tolstoy and the brothers Zhemchuzhnikovy, ed.

[131](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

I remember that Szigeti, the violinist, once asked me how many pupils I had and when I told him “about thirty” he cried out, aghast, “But this is suicide! ”.

[132](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

Greek musician and poet who lived in Lesbos in the VIIth century b. g. and is believed to have been the first to introduce the heptachord, ed.

[133](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

The same may be said of the failure to appreciate a great contemporary work (to mention but Shostakovich’s Eighth Symphony).

[134](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

Of course the same may be said of any great man, in any case of a learned man.

[135](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

I have it from Artur Rubinstein himself. They met in a train and travelled in the same compartment.

[136](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

Obviously by “universality” I do not mean a mastery of the entire piano literature quantitatively speaking, but qualitatively.

[137](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

That is why I call this the “mortuary” style. Sometimes this style is mistakenly referred to as the “cerebral” style. This is a regrettable misunderstanding. I have the utmost respect for the brain, and the utmost distaste for the mortuary.

[138](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

A word which Busoni hated. He considered that it could be applied to an instrument but not to a person.

[139](part0013.html#CCNA1-37801cf57157419e93617688715271e0)

This awareness considerably softens my own personal requirements as a teacher, but, of course, in cases when it is already possible to engage in discussion with a pupil and not merely give him instructions.
